{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01GQVEnfADSxLpLRAnNvKEWQ","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2: Copyright 2014 The Kubernetes Authors.\\n3: \\n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \\\"License\\\");\\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\\n7: \\n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\\n9: \\n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \\\"AS IS\\\" BASIS,\\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\\n14: limitations under the License.\\n15: */\\n16: \\n17: package cache\\n18: \\n19: import (\\n20: \\t\\\"errors\\\"\\n21: \\t\\\"fmt\\\"\\n22: \\t\\\"sync\\\"\\n23: \\t\\\"time\\\"\\n24: \\n25: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/sets\\\"\\n26: \\n27: \\t\\\"k8s.io/klog/v2\\\"\\n28: \\tutiltrace \\\"k8s.io/utils/trace\\\"\\n29: )\\n30: \\n31: // DeltaFIFOOptions is the configuration parameters for DeltaFIFO. All are\\n32: // optional.\\n33: type DeltaFIFOOptions struct {\\n34: \\n35: \\t// KeyFunction is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It's\\n36: \\t// exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional\\n37: \\t// handling around deleted objects and queue state).\\n38: \\t// Optional, the default is MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\\n39: \\tKeyFunction KeyFunc\\n40: \\n41: \\t// KnownObjects is expected to return a list of keys that the consumer of\\n42: \\t// this queue \\\"knows about\\\". It is used to decide which items are missing\\n43: \\t// when Replace() is called; 'Deleted' deltas are produced for the missing items.\\n44: \\t// KnownObjects may be nil if you can tolerate missing deletions on Replace().\\n45: \\tKnownObjects KeyListerGetter\\n46: \\n47: \\t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced indicates that the queue consumer\\n48: \\t// understands the Replaced DeltaType. Before the `Replaced` event type was\\n49: \\t// added, calls to Replace() were handled the same as Sync(). For\\n50: \\t// backwards-compatibility purposes, this is false by default.\\n51: \\t// When true, `Replaced` events will be sent for items passed to a Replace() call.\\n52: \\t// When false, `Sync` events will be sent instead.\\n53: \\tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\\n54: \\n55: \\t// If set, will be called for objects before enqueueing them. Please\\n56: \\t// see the comment on TransformFunc for details.\\n57: \\tTransformer TransformFunc\\n58: }\\n59: \\n60: // DeltaFIFO is like FIFO, but differs in two ways.  One is that the\\n61: // accumulator associated with a given object's key is not that object\\n62: // but rather a Deltas, which is a slice of Delta values for that\\n63: // object.  Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\\n64: // except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\\n65: // Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\\n66: // not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\\n67: // Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\\n68: // DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\\n69: //\\n70: // The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\\n71: // an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\\n72: // If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\\n73: // replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\\n74: // resync events.\\n75: //\\n76: // DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\\n77: // intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\\n78: // the Pop() method.\\n79: //\\n80: // DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\\n81: //   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\\n82: //   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\\n83: //     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\\n84: //   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\\n85: //   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\\n86: //\\n87: // DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\\n88: // interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\\n89: // will always return an object of type Deltas. List() returns\\n90: // the newest object from each accumulator in the FIFO.\\n91: //\\n92: // A DeltaFIFO's knownObjects KeyListerGetter provides the abilities\\n93: // to list Store keys and to get objects by Store key.  The objects in\\n94: // question are called \\\"known objects\\\" and this set of objects\\n95: // modifies the behavior of the Delete, Replace, and Resync methods\\n96: // (each in a different way).\\n97: //\\n98: // A note on threading: If you call Pop() in parallel from multiple\\n99: // threads, you could end up with multiple threads processing slightly\\n100: // different versions of the same object.\\n101: type DeltaFIFO struct {\\n102: \\t// lock/cond protects access to 'items' and 'queue'.\\n103: \\tlock sync.RWMutex\\n104: \\tcond sync.Cond\\n105: \\n106: \\t// `items` maps a key to a Deltas.\\n107: \\t// Each such Deltas has at least one Delta.\\n108: \\titems map[string]Deltas\\n109: \\n110: \\t// `queue` maintains FIFO order of keys for consumption in Pop().\\n111: \\t// There are no duplicates in `queue`.\\n112: \\t// A key is in `queue` if and only if it is in `items`.\\n113: \\tqueue []string\\n114: \\n115: \\t// populated is true if the first batch of items inserted by Replace() has been populated\\n116: \\t// or Delete/Add/Update/AddIfNotPresent was called first.\\n117: \\tpopulated bool\\n118: \\t// initialPopulationCount is the number of items inserted by the first call of Replace()\\n119: \\tinitialPopulationCount int\\n120: \\n121: \\t// keyFunc is used to make the key used for queued item\\n122: \\t// insertion and retrieval, and should be deterministic.\\n123: \\tkeyFunc KeyFunc\\n124: \\n125: \\t// knownObjects list keys that are \\\"known\\\" --- affecting Delete(),\\n126: \\t// Replace(), and Resync()\\n127: \\tknownObjects KeyListerGetter\\n128: \\n129: \\t// Used to indicate a queue is closed so a control loop can exit when a queue is empty.\\n130: \\t// Currently, not used to gate any of CRUD operations.\\n131: \\tclosed bool\\n132: \\n133: \\t// emitDeltaTypeReplaced is whether to emit the Replaced or Sync\\n134: \\t// DeltaType when Replace() is called (to preserve backwards compat).\\n135: \\temitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\\n136: \\n137: \\t// Called with every object if non-nil.\\n138: \\ttransformer TransformFunc\\n139: }\\n140: \\n141: // TransformFunc allows for transforming an object before it will be processed.\\n142: //\\n143: // The most common usage pattern is to clean-up some parts of the object to\\n144: // reduce component memory usage if a given component doesn't care about them.\\n145: //\\n146: // New in v1.27: TransformFunc sees the object before any other actor, and it\\n147: // is now safe to mutate the object in place instead of making a copy.\\n148: //\\n149: // It's recommended for the TransformFunc to be idempotent.\\n150: // It MUST be idempotent if objects already present in the cache are passed to\\n151: // the Replace() to avoid re-mutating them. Default informers do not pass\\n152: // existing objects to Replace though.\\n153: //\\n154: // Note that TransformFunc is called while inserting objects into the\\n155: // notification queue and is therefore extremely performance sensitive; please\\n156: // do not do anything that will take a long time.\\n157: type TransformFunc func(interface{}) (interface{}, error)\\n158: \\n159: // DeltaType is the type of a change (addition, deletion, etc)\\n160: type DeltaType string\\n161: \\n162: // Change type definition\\n163: const (\\n164: \\tAdded   DeltaType = \\\"Added\\\"\\n165: \\tUpdated DeltaType = \\\"Updated\\\"\\n166: \\tDeleted DeltaType = \\\"Deleted\\\"\\n167: \\t// Replaced is emitted when we encountered watch errors and had to do a\\n168: \\t// relist. We don't know if the replaced object has changed.\\n169: \\t//\\n170: \\t// NOTE: Previous versions of DeltaFIFO would use Sync for Replace events\\n171: \\t// as well. Hence, Replaced is only emitted when the option\\n172: \\t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is true.\\n173: \\tReplaced DeltaType = \\\"Replaced\\\"\\n174: \\t// Sync is for synthetic events during a periodic resync.\\n175: \\tSync DeltaType = \\\"Sync\\\"\\n176: )\\n177: \\n178: // Delta is a member of Deltas (a list of Delta objects) which\\n179: // in its turn is the type stored by a DeltaFIFO. It tells you what\\n180: // change happened, and the object's state after* that change.\\n181: //\\n182: // [*] Unless the change is a deletion, and then you'll get the final\\n183: // state of the object before it was deleted.\\n184: type Delta struct {\\n185: \\tType   DeltaType\\n186: \\tObject interface{}\\n187: }\\n188: \\n189: // Deltas is a list of one or more 'Delta's to an individual object.\\n190: // The oldest delta is at index 0, the newest delta is the last one.\\n191: type Deltas []Delta\\n192: \\n193: // NewDeltaFIFO returns a Queue which can be used to process changes to items.\\n194: //\\n195: // keyFunc is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It is\\n196: // exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional handling\\n197: // around deleted objects and queue state).\\n198: //\\n199: // 'knownObjects' may be supplied to modify the behavior of Delete,\\n200: // Replace, and Resync.  It may be nil if you do not need those\\n201: // modifications.\\n202: //\\n203: // TODO: consider merging keyLister with this object, tracking a list of\\n204: // \\\"known\\\" keys when Pop() is called. Have to think about how that\\n205: // affects error retrying.\\n206: //\\n207: //\\tNOTE: It is possible to misuse this and cause a race when using an\\n208: //\\texternal known object source.\\n209: //\\tWhether there is a potential race depends on how the consumer\\n210: //\\tmodifies knownObjects. In Pop(), process function is called under\\n211: //\\tlock, so it is safe to update data structures in it that need to be\\n212: //\\tin sync with the queue (e.g. knownObjects).\\n213: //\\n214: //\\tExample:\\n215: //\\tIn case of sharedIndexInformer being a consumer\\n216: //\\t(https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/blob/0cdd940f/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/shared_informer.go#L192),\\n217: //\\tthere is no race as knownObjects (s.indexer) is modified safely\\n218: //\\tunder DeltaFIFO's lock. The only exceptions are GetStore() and\\n219: //\\tGetIndexer() methods, which expose ways to modify the underlying\\n220: //\\tstorage. Currently these two methods are used for creating Lister\\n221: //\\tand internal tests.\\n222: //\\n223: // Also see the comment on DeltaFIFO.\\n224: //\\n225: // Warning: This constructs a DeltaFIFO that does not differentiate between\\n226: // events caused by a call to Replace (e.g., from a relist, which may\\n227: // contain object updates), and synthetic events caused by a periodic resync\\n228: // (which just emit the existing object). All are\\n32: // optional.\\n33: type DeltaFIFOOptions struct {\\n34: \\n35: \\t// KeyFunction is used to figure out what key an object should have. For\\n50: \\t// backwards-compatibility purposes, this is false by default.\\n51: \\t// When true, `Replaced` events will be sent for items passed to a Replace() call.\\n52: \\t// When false, `Sync` events will be sent instead.\\n53: \\tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\\n54: \\n55: \\t// If set, will be called for objects before enqueueing them. Please\\n56: \\t// see the comment on TransformFunc for details.\\n57: \\tTransformer TransformFunc\\n58: }\\n59: \\n60: // DeltaFIFO is like FIFO, but differs in two ways.  One is that the\\n61: // accumulator associated with a given object's key is not that object\\n62: // but rather a Deltas, which is a slice of Delta values for that\\n63: // object.  Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\\n64: // except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\\n65: // Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\\n66: // not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\\n67: // Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\\n68: // DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\\n69: //\\n70: // The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\\n71: // an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\\n72: // If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\\n73: // replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\\n74: // resync events.\\n75: //\\n76: // DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\\n77: // intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\\n78: // the Pop() method.\\n79: //\\n80: // DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\\n81: //   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\\n82: //   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\\n83: //     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\\n84: //   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\\n85: //   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\\n86: //\\n87: // DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\\n88: // interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\\n89: // will always return an object of type Deltas. List() returns\\n90: // the newest object from each accumulator in the FIFO.\\n91: //\\n92: // A DeltaFIFO's knownObjects KeyListerGetter provides the abilities\\n93: // to list Store keys and to get objects by Store key. way).\\n97: //\\n98: // A note on threading: If you call Pop() in parallel from multiple\\n99: // threads, you could end up with multiple threads processing slightly\\n100: // different versions of It tells you what\n180: // change happened, and the object's state after* that change.\n181: //\n182: // [*] Unless the change is a deletion, and then you'll get the final\n183: // state of the object before it was deleted.\n184: type Delta struct {\n185: \tType   DeltaType\n186: \tObject interface{}\n187: }\n188: \n189: // Deltas is a list of one or more 'Delta's to an individual object.\n190: // The oldest delta is at index 0, the newest delta is the last one.\n191: type Deltas []Delta\n192: \n193: // NewDeltaFIFO returns a Queue which can be used to process changes to items.\n194: //\n195: // keyFunc is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It is\n196: // exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional handling\n197: // around deleted objects and queue state).\n198: //\n199: // 'knownObjects' may be supplied to modify the behavior of Delete,\n200: // Replace, and Resync.  It may be nil if you do not need those\n201: // modifications.\n202: //\n203: // TODO: consider merging keyLister with this object, tracking a list of\n204: // \"known\" keys when Pop() is called. Have to think about how that\n205: // affects error retrying.\n206: //\n207: //\tNOTE: It is possible to misuse this and cause a race when using an\n208: //\texternal known object source.\n209: //\tWhether there is a potential race depends on how the consumer\n210: //\tmodifies knownObjects. In Pop(), process function is called under\n211: //\tlock, so it is safe to update data structures in it that need to be\n212: //\tin sync with the queue (e.g. knownObjects).\n213: //\n214: //\tExample:\n215: //\tIn case of sharedIndexInformer being a consumer\n216: //\t(https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/blob/0cdd940f/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/shared_informer.go#L192),\n217: //\tthere is no race as knownObjects (s.indexer) is modified safely\n218: //\tunder DeltaFIFO's lock. The only exceptions are GetStore() and\n219: //\tGetIndexer() methods, which expose ways to modify the underlying\n220: //\tstorage. Currently these two methods are used for creating Lister\n221: //\tand internal tests.\n222: //\n223: // Also see the comment on DeltaFIFO.\n224: //\n225: // Warning: This constructs a DeltaFIFO that does not differentiate between\n226: // events caused by a call to Replace (e.g., from a relist, which may\n227: // contain object updates), and synthetic events caused by a periodic resync\n228: // (which just emit the existing object). See https://issue.k8s.io/86015 for details.\n229: //\n230: // Use `NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{..., EmitDeltaTypeReplaced: true})`\n231: // instead to receive a `Replaced` event depending on the type.\n232: //\n233: // Deprecated: Equivalent to NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{KeyFunction: keyFunc, KnownObjects: knownObjects})\n234: func NewDeltaFIFO(keyFunc KeyFunc, knownObjects KeyListerGetter) *DeltaFIFO {\n235: \treturn NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{\n236: \t\tKeyFunction:  keyFunc,\n237: \t\tKnownObjects: knownObjects,\n238: \t})\n239: }\n240: \n241: // NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions returns a Queue which can be used to process changes to\n242: // items. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_012oY81WVaVYBQXDAsZdPjrK","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\\n3: \\n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \\\"License\\\");\\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\\n7: \\n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\\n9: \\n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \\\"AS IS\\\" BASIS,\\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\\n14: limitations under the License.\\n15: */\\n16: \\n17: package cache\\n18: \\n19: import (\\n20: \\t\\\"errors\\\"\\n21: \\t\\\"fmt\\\"\\n22: \\t\\\"sync\\\"\\n23: \\t\\\"time\\\"\\n24: \\n25: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/meta\\\"\\n26: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime\\\"\\n27: \\tutilruntime \\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\\\"\\n28: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\\\"\\n29: \\t\\\"k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/synctrack\\\"\\n30: \\t\\\"k8s.io/utils/buffer\\\"\\n31: \\t\\\"k8s.io/utils/clock\\\"\\n32: \\n33: \\t\\\"k8s.io/klog/v2\\\"\\n34: \\n35: \\tclientgofeaturegate \\\"k8s.io/client-go/features\\\"\\n36: )\\n37: \\n38: // SharedInformer provides eventually consistent linkage of its\\n39: // clients to the authoritative state of a given collection of\\n40: // objects.  An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\\n41: // namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\\n42: // an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\\n43: // SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\\n44: // group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\\n45: // SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\\n46: // applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\\n47: //\\n48: // The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\\n49: // access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\\n50: // An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\\n51: // other appropriate content or (2) \\\"absent\\\".\\n52: //\\n53: // A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\\n54: // by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\\n55: // machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\\n56: // the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\\n57: // consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\\n58: // prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\\n59: // particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\\n60: // then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\\n61: // eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\\n62: // state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\\n63: // service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\\n64: // absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\\n65: // selector.\\n66: //\\n67: // For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\\n68: // states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\\n69: // states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\\n70: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\\n71: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\\n72: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\\n73: //\\n74: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\\n75: // during `Run()`.\\n76: //\\n77: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\\n78: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\\n79: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\\n80: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\\n81: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\\n82: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\\n83: // persistently thwart achievement).\\n84: //\\n85: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\\n86: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\\n87: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\\n88: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\\n89: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\\n90: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\\n91: //\\n92: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\\n93: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\\n94: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\\n95: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\\n96: // into its constituent parts.\\n97: //\\n98: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\\n99: // snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\\n100: // will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\\n101: //\\n102: // A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\\n103: // update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\\n104: // added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\\n105: // stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\\n106: // after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\\n107: // additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\\n108: // client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\\n109: // local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\\n110: // SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\\n111: // update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\\n112: // update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\\n113: // corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\\n114: // and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\\n115: // For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\\n116: // delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\\n117: // object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\\n118: // `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\\n119: // that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\\n120: // `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\\n121: // and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\\n122: // created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\\n123: // rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\\n124: // need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\\n125: // field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\\n126: // notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\\n127: //\\n128: // A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\\n129: // is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\\n130: // notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\\n131: // to something else, for example through a\\n132: // `client-go/util/workqueue`.\\n133: //\\n134: // A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\\n135: // state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\\n136: // ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\\n137: type SharedInformer interface {\\n138: \\t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\\n139: \\t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\\n140: \\t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\\n141: \\t// different handlers.\\n142: \\t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\\n143: \\t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\\n144: \\t// seen every item in the initial list).\\n145: \\tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\\n146: \\t// AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod adds an event handler to the\\n147: \\t// shared informer with the requested resync period; zero means\\n148: \\t// this handler does not care about resyncs.  The resync operation\\n149: \\t// consists of delivering to the handler an update notification\\n150: \\t// for every object in the informer's local cache; it does not add\\n151: \\t// any interactions with the authoritative storage.  Some\\n152: \\t// informers do no resyncs at all, not even for handlers added\\n153: \\t// with a non-zero resyncPeriod.  For an informer that does\\n154: \\t// resyncs, and for each handler that requests resyncs, that\\n155: \\t// informer develops a nominal resync period that is no shorter\\n156: \\t// than the requested period but may be longer.  The actual time\\n157: \\t// between any two resyncs may be longer than the nominal period\\n158: \\t// because the implementation takes time to do work and there may\\n159: \\t// be competing load and scheduling noise.\\n160: \\t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to remove\\n161: \\t// the handler again and an error if the handler cannot be added.\\n162: \\tAddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod(handler ResourceEventHandler, resyncPeriod time.Duration) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\\n163: \\t// RemoveEventHandler removes a formerly added event handler given by\\n164: \\t// its registration handle.\\n165: \\t// This function is guaranteed to be idempotent, and thread-safe.\\n166: \\tRemoveEventHandler(handle ResourceEventHandlerRegistration) error\\n167: \\t// GetStore returns the informer's local cache as a Store.\\n168: \\tGetStore() Store\\n169: \\t// GetController is deprecated, it does nothing useful\\n170: \\tGetController() Controller\\n171: \\t// Run starts and runs the shared informer, returning after it stops.\\n172: \\t// The informer will be stopped when stopCh is closed.\\n173: \\tRun(stopCh <-chan struct{})\\n174: \\t// HasSynced returns true if the shared informer's store has been\\n175: \\t// informed by at least one full LIST of the authoritative state\\n176: \\t// of the informer's object collection.  This is unrelated to \\\"resync\\\".\\n177: \\t//\\n178: \\t// Note that this doesn't tell you if an individual handler is synced!!\\n179: \\t// For that, please call HasSynced on the handle returned by\\n180: \\t// AddEventHandler.\\n181: \\tHasSynced() bool\\n182: \\t// LastSyncResourceVersion is the resource version observed when last synced with the underlying\\n183: \\t// store. The value returned is not synchronized with access to the underlying store and is not\\n184: \\t// thread-safe.\\n185: \\tLastSyncResourceVersion() string\\n186: \\n187: \\t// The WatchErrorHandler is called whenever ListAndWatch drops the\\n188: \\t// connection with an error. After calling this handler, the informer\\n189: \\t// will backoff and retry.\\n190: \\t//\\n191: \\t// The default implementation looks at the error type and tries to log\\n192: \\t// the error message at an appropriate level.\\n193: \\t//\\n194: \\t// There's only one handler, so if you call this multiple times, last one\\n195: \\t// wins; calling after the informer has been started returns an error.\\n196: \\t//\\n197: \\t// The handler is intended for visibility, not to e.g. pause the consumers.\\n198: \\t// The handler should return quickly - any expensive processing should be\\n199: \\t// offloaded.\\n200: \\tSetWatchErrorHandler(handler WatchErrorHandler) error\\n201: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0@8e5772e5b95a59b265a3b48c5fe5a7d1e163cf69/-/blob/tools/cache/shared_informer.go%3FL1-200\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"b475a84a-58e0-4123-97fc-2483030bcddc","uuid":"6328526d-b93c-4f9e-b8a5-136c19e74915","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\\n3: \\n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \\\"License\\\");\\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\\n7: \\n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\\n9: \\n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \\\"AS IS\\\" BASIS,\\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\\n14: limitations under the License.\\n15: */\\n16: \\n17: package cache\\n18: \\n19: import (\\n20: \\t\\\"errors\\\"\\n21: \\t\\\"fmt\\\"\\n22: \\t\\\"sync\\\"\\n23: \\t\\\"time\\\"\\n24: \\n25: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/meta\\\"\\n26: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime\\\"\\n27: \\tutilruntime \\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\\\"\\n28: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\\\"\\n29: \\t\\\"k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/synctrack\\\"\\n30: \\t\\\"k8s.io/utils/buffer\\\"\\n31: \\t\\\"k8s.io/utils/clock\\\"\\n32: \\n33: \\t\\\"k8s.io/klog/v2\\\"\\n34: \\n35: \\tclientgofeaturegate \\\"k8s.io/client-go/features\\\"\\n36: )\\n37: \\n38: // SharedInformer provides eventually consistent linkage of its\\n39: // clients to the authoritative state of a given collection of\\n40: // objects.  An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\\n41: // namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\\n42: // an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\\n43: // SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\\n44: // group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\\n45: // SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\\n46: // applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\\n47: //\\n48: // The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\\n49: // access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\\n50: // An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\\n51: // other appropriate content or (2) \\\"absent\\\".\\n52: //\\n53: // A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\\n54: // by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\\n55: // machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\\n56: // the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\\n57: // consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\\n58: // prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\\n59: // particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\\n60: // then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\\n61: // eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\\n62: // state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\\n63: // service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\\n64: // absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\\n65: // selector.\\n66: //\\n67: // For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\\n68: // states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\\n69: // states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\\n70: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\\n71: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\\n72: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\\n73: //\\n74: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\\n75: // during `Run()`.\\n76: //\\n77: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\\n78: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\\n79: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\\n80: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\\n81: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\\n82: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\\n83: // persistently thwart achievement).\\n84: //\\n85: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\\n86: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\\n87: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\\n88: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\\n89: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\\n90: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\\n91: //\\n92: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\\n93: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\\n94: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\\n95: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\\n96: // into its constituent parts.\\n97: //\\n98: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\\n99: // snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\\n100: // will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\\n101: //\\n102: // A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\\n103: // update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\\n104: // added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\\n105: // stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\\n106: // after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\\n107: // additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\\n108: // client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\\n109: // local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\\n110: // SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\\n111: // update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\\n112: // update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\\n113: // corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\\n114: // and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\\n115: // For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\\n116: // delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\\n117: // object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\\n118: // `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\\n119: // that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\\n120: // `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\\n121: // and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\\n122: // created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\\n123: // rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\\n124: // need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\\n125: // field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\\n126: // notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\\n127: //\\n128: // A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\\n129: // is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\\n130: // notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\\n131: // to something else, for example through a\\n132: // `client-go/util/workqueue`.\\n133: //\\n134: // A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\\n135: // state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\\n136: // ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\\n137: type SharedInformer interface {\\n138: \\t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\\n139: \\t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\\n140: \\t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\\n141: \\t// different handlers.\\n142: \\t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\\n143: \\t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\\n144: \\t// seen every item in the initial list).\\n145: \\tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\\n146: \\t// AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod adds an event handler to the\\n147: \\t// shared informer with the requested resync period; zero means\\n148: \\t// this handler does not care about resyncs.  The resync operation\\n149: \\t// consists of delivering to the handler an update notification\\n150: \\t// for every object in the informer's local cache; it does not add\\n151: \\t// any interactions with the authoritative storage.  Some\\n152: \\t// informers do no resyncs at all, not even for handlers added\\n153: \\t// with a non-zero resyncPeriod.  For an informer that does\\n154: \\t// resyncs, and for each handler that requests resyncs, that\\n155: \\t// informer develops a nominal resync period that is no shorter\\n156: \\t// than the requested period but may be longer.  The actual time\\n157: \\t// between any two resyncs may be longer than the nominal period\\n158: \\t// because the implementation takes time to do work and there may\\n159: \\t// be competing load and scheduling noise.\\n160: \\t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to remove\\n161: \\t// the handler again and an error if the handler cannot be added.\\n162: \\tAddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod(handler ResourceEventHandler, resyncPeriod time.Duration) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\\n163: \\t// RemoveEventHandler removes a formerly added event handler given by\\n164: \\t// its registration handle.\\n165: \\t// This function is guaranteed to be idempotent, and thread-safe.\\n166: \\tRemoveEventHandler(handle ResourceEventHandlerRegistration) error\\n167: \\t// GetStore returns the informer's local cache as a Store.\\n168: \\tGetStore() Store\\n169: \\t// GetController is deprecated, it does nothing useful\\n170: \\tGetController() Controller\\n171: \\t// Run starts and runs the shared informer, returning after it stops.\\n172: \\t// The informer will be stopped when stopCh is closed.\\n173: \\tRun(stopCh <-chan struct{})\\n174: \\t// HasSynced returns true if the shared informer's store has been\\n175: \\t// informed by at least one full LIST of the authoritative state\\n176: \\t// of the informer's object collection. This will require a little thought\\n186: // to make sure that we don't end up processing the same object multiple times\\n187: // concurrently.\\n188: //\\n189: // TODO: Plumb through the stopCh here (and down to the queue) so that this can\\n190: // actually exit when the controller is stopped. Or just give up on this stuff\\n191: // ever being stoppable. Converting this whole package to use Context would\\n192: // also be helpful.\\n193: func (c *controller) processLoop() {\\n194: \\tfor {\\n195: \\t\\tobj, err := c.config.Queue.Pop(PopProcessFunc(c.config.Process))\\n196: \\t\\tif err != nil {\\n197: \\t\\t\\tif err == ErrFIFOClosed {\\n198: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn\\n199: \\t\\t\\t}\\n200: \\t\\t\\tif c.config.RetryOnError {\\n201: \\t\\t\\t\\t// This is the safe way to re-enqueue.\\n202: \\t\\t\\t\\tc.config.Queue.AddIfNotPresent(obj)\\n203: \\t\\t\\t}\\n204: \\t\\t}\\n205: \\t}\\n206: }\\n207: \\n208: // ResourceEventHandler can handle notifications for events that\\n209: // happen to a resource. If\n563: // multiple items are ready, they are returned in the order in which they were\n564: // added/updated. A\\n28: // Store holds a map from string keys to accumulators, and has\\n29: // operations to add, update, and delete a given object to/from the\\n30: // accumulator currently associated with a given key.  A Store also\\n31: // knows how to extract the key from a given object, so many operations\\n32: // are given only the object.\\n33: //\\n34: // In the simplest Store implementations each accumulator is simply\\n35: // the last given object, or empty after Delete, and thus the Store's\\n36: // behavior is simple storage.\\n37: //\\n38: // Reflector knows how to watch a server and update a Store.  This\\n39: // package provides a variety of implementations of Store.\\n40: type Store interface {\\n41: \\n42: \\t// Add adds the given object to the accumulator associated with the given object's key\\n43: \\tAdd(obj interface{}) error\\n44: \\n45: \\t// Update updates the given object in the accumulator associated with the given object's key\\n46: \\tUpdate(obj interface{}) error\\n47: \\n48: \\t// Delete deletes the given object from the accumulator associated with the given object's key\\n49: \\tDelete(obj interface{}) error\\n50: \\n51: \\t// List returns a list of all the currently non-empty accumulators\\n52: \\tList() []interface{}\\n53: \\n54: \\t// ListKeys returns a list of all the keys currently associated with non-empty accumulators\\n55: \\tListKeys() []string\\n56: \\n57: \\t// Get returns the accumulator associated with the given object's key\\n58: \\tGet(obj interface{}) (item interface{}, exists bool, err error)\\n59: \\n60: \\t// GetByKey returns the accumulator associated with the given key\\n61: \\tGetByKey(key string) (item interface{}, exists bool, err error)\\n62: \\n63: \\t// Replace will delete the contents of the store, using instead the\\n64: \\t// given list. Store takes ownership of the list, you should not reference\\n65: \\t// it after calling this function.\\n66: \\tReplace([]interface{}, string) error\\n67: \\n68: \\t// Resync is meaningless in the terms appearing here but has\\n69: \\t// meaning in some implementations that have non-trivial\\n70: \\t// additional behavior (e.g., DeltaFIFO).\\n71: \\tResync() error\\n72: }\\n73: \\n74: // KeyFunc knows how to make a key from an object. Implementations should be deterministic.\\n75: type KeyFunc func(obj interface{}) (string, error)\\n76: \\n77: // KeyError will be returned any time a KeyFunc gives an error; it includes the object\\n78: // at fault.\\n79: type KeyError struct {\\n80: \\tObj interface{}\\n81: \\tErr error\\n82: }\\n83: \\n84: // Error gives a human-readable description of the error.\\n85: func (k Now I have all the pieces. Let me compile my findings:\n\nThe complete event handler chain from API server to informer cache updates:\n\n1. **ListWatch** (tools/cache/listwatch.go) - Provides List() and Watch() interfaces to consume API server events\n\n2. **Reflector** (tools/cache/reflector.go):\n   - Run() - starts the reflector loop\n   - ListAndWatch() - coordinates initial list and watches\n   - list() - calls lw.List() to get initial list\n   - watch() - calls lw.Watch() to get watch stream\n   - handleAnyWatch() - processes watch events from the watch stream\n   - Reflector feeds events to DeltaFIFO via store.Add(), store.Update(), store.Delete()\n\n3. **DeltaFIFO** (tools/cache/delta_fifo.go) - Queue implementation that:\n   - Add() - creates Added delta\n   - Update() - creates Updated delta\n   - Delete() - creates Deleted delta\n   - Replace() - syncs initial list (creates Sync or Replaced deltas)\n   - Pop() - returns Deltas objects to be processed\n\n4. **Controller** (tools/cache/controller.go):\n   - Run() - creates Reflector and starts processLoop\n   - processLoop() - calls Queue.Pop() with Process function\n   - Process function calls processDeltas()\n   - processDeltas() - processes each delta and calls handler methods:\n     - handler.OnAdd()\n     - handler.OnUpdate()\n     - handler.OnDelete()\n\n5. **sharedIndexInformer** (tools/cache/shared_informer.go):\n   - Implements ResourceEventHandler with OnAdd(), OnUpdate(), OnDelete() methods\n   - These methods call processor.distribute() to send notifications\n   - Updates the indexer (cache.Store) at the same time\n\n6. **sharedProcessor** (tools/cache/shared_informer.go):\n   - distribute() - sends notifications to all processorListeners\n   - Has a map of listeners\n\n7. **processorListener** (tools/cache/shared_informer.go):\n   - Holds a ResourceEventHandler (user's handler)\n   - Has channels nextCh and addCh\n   - pop() goroutine pumps from addCh to nextCh through a ring buffer\n   - run() goroutine receives from nextCh and calls handler.OnAdd(), OnUpdate(), OnDelete()\n\nThe full chain flows from API Server Watch through ListWatch.Watch() into Reflector.watch(), which processes events and feeds them through DeltaFIFO to the Controller's processLoop. server watch stream through the client-go informer machinery to user-registered event handlers.\\n\\n**1. ListWatch Interface (tools/cache/listwatch.go):**\\nThe ListWatch struct implements the ListerWatcher interface with two core methods:\\n- Watch(): Establishes a watch stream with the API server that streams watch.Event objects\\n- List(): Performs an initial list of objects from the API server\\n\\n**2. Reflector (tools/cache/reflector.go):**\\nThe Reflector watches a specified resource and reflects changes into a store. Key methods:\\n- Run(): Entry point that calls ListAndWatch() in a retry loop\\n- ListAndWatch(): Orchestrates initial list via Reflector.list() and then watch via watchWithResync()\\n- handleAnyWatch(): Processes individual watch events from w.ResultChan() by calling store.Add(), store.Update(), or store.Delete() based on event.Type (watch.Added, watch.Modified, watch.Deleted)\\n\\n**3. DeltaFIFO Queue (tools/cache/delta_fifo.go):**\\nA queue that stores Deltas (lists of Delta objects representing state changes). Key methods:\\n- Add(obj): Creates an Added delta and enqueues it\\n- Update(obj): Creates an Updated delta and enqueues it\\n- Delete(obj): Creates a Deleted delta and enqueues it\\n- Replace(list): Syncs initial list by creating Sync/Replaced deltas and detecting deletions\\n- Pop(process): Dequeues a Deltas object and calls the process function (in the same critical section)\\n\\nDeltaFIFO accumulates all changes to an object as a Deltas slice, allowing consumers to see the complete history of changes while the queue was processing.\\n\\n**4. Controller (tools/cache/controller.go):**\\nLow-level controller that orchestrates Reflector and DeltaFIFO. Key methods:\\n- Run(): Creates Reflector with the ListerWatcher and Queue, starts Reflector.Run() and processLoop()\\n- processLoop(): Continuously calls Queue.Pop() with the Process function\\n- The Process function extracts Deltas and calls processDeltas()\\n- processDeltas(handler, store, deltas): Iterates through each Delta and:\\n  - Updates the local store (indexer)\\n  - Calls handler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList) for Added/Sync/Replaced deltas\\n  - Calls handler.OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj) for Updated deltas on existing objects\\n  - Calls handler.OnDelete(obj) for Deleted deltas\\n\\n**5. SharedIndexInformer (tools/cache/shared_informer.go):**\\nImplements SharedInformer interface and acts as the main event handler. Key components:\\n- sharedIndexInformer struct: Contains indexer (cache.Store) and sharedProcessor\\n- HandleDeltas(obj): Called by processDeltas via controller, receives Deltas from DeltaFIFO, calls processDeltas() which invokes OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete\\n- OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList): Updates indexer and calls processor.distribute(addNotification{newObj, isInInitialList}, false)\\n- OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj): Updates indexer and calls processor.distribute(updateNotification{oldObj, newObj}, isSync)\\n- OnDelete(obj): Updates indexer and calls processor.distribute(deleteNotification{oldObj}, false)\\n\\n**6. SharedProcessor (tools/cache/shared_informer.go):**\\nResponsible for dispatching notifications to all registered event listeners. Key methods:\\n- distribute(notification, sync): Iterates through all listeners (processorListener instances) and calls listener.add(notification)\\n- Each listener receives the notification asynchronously\\n\\n**7. ProcessorListener (tools/cache/shared_informer.go):**\\nRelays notifications from sharedProcessor to one ResourceEventHandler using two goroutines and channels. Key components:\\n- handler: The actual ResourceEventHandler registered by the user (implements OnAdd, OnUpdate, OnDelete)\\n- addCh: Receives notifications from processor.distribute()\\n- nextCh: Buffers notifications for the run() goroutine\\n- pendingNotifications: Ring buffer for notifications not yet dispatched\\n\\nKey goroutines:\\n- pop(): Pumps notifications from addCh to nextCh using the ring buffer, handling backpressure when nextCh is not keeping up\\n- run(): Receives notifications from nextCh and dispatches them:\\n  - addNotification → calls handler.OnAdd(newObj, isInInitialList)\\n  - updateNotification → calls handler.OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj)\\n  - deleteNotification → calls handler.OnDelete(oldObj)\\n\\n**Complete Event Flow:**\\n1. API Server streams watch events → ListWatch.Watch() receives events\\n2. Reflector.watch() calls handleAnyWatch() to consume events\\n3. handleAnyWatch() calls store.Add/Update/Delete() for each watch event (DeltaFIFO)\\n4. DeltaFIFO creates Delta objects and enqueues them\\n5. Controller.processLoop() pops Deltas from DeltaFIFO\\n6. processDeltas() processes each Delta and calls sharedIndexInformer.OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete\\n7. sharedIndexInformer updates indexer (cache) and calls processor.distribute()\\n8. processor sends notifications to all processorListeners\\n9. processorListener.pop() buffers notifications, processorListener.run() dispatches them\\n10. Finally calls user's registered ResourceEventHandler methods (OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete)\\n\\nThis multi-stage pipeline with buffering, synchronization points, and handler isolation ensures that:\\n- Watch events are reliably processed\\n- The local cache is always consistent\\n- Event handlers run asynchronously and independently\\n- Multiple handlers can be registered without blocking each other\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1447,"cache_read_input_tokens":97599,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1447},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"b475a84a-58e0-4123-97fc-2483030bcddc","uuid":"c7115329-727f-4568-9535-17160d8d5359"}

\"path\": \"tools/cache/shared_informer.go\", \"symbol\": \"processorListener.run\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The Kubernetes informer cache event handler chain traces the flow of events from the API server watch stream through the client-go informer machinery to user-registered event handlers.\\n\\n**1. ListWatch Interface (tools/cache/listwatch.go):**\\nThe ListWatch struct implements the ListerWatcher interface with two core methods:\\n- Watch(): Establishes a watch stream with the API server that streams watch.Event objects\\n- List(): Performs an initial list of objects from the API server\\n\\n**2. Reflector (tools/cache/reflector.go):**\\nThe Reflector watches a specified resource and reflects changes into a store. Key methods:\\n- Run(): Entry point that calls ListAndWatch() in a retry loop\\n- ListAndWatch(): Orchestrates initial list via Reflector.list() and then watch via watchWithResync()\\n- handleAnyWatch(): Processes individual watch events from w.ResultChan() by calling store.Add(), store.Update(), or store.Delete() based on event.Type (watch.Added, watch.Modified, watch.Deleted)\\n\\n**3. DeltaFIFO Queue (tools/cache/delta_fifo.go):**\\nA queue that stores Deltas (lists of Delta objects representing state changes). Key methods:\\n- Add(obj): Creates an Added delta and enqueues it\\n- Update(obj): Creates an Updated delta and enqueues it\\n- Delete(obj): Creates a Deleted delta and enqueues it\\n- Replace(list): Syncs initial list by creating Sync/Replaced deltas and detecting deletions\\n- Pop(process): Dequeues a Deltas object and calls the process function (in the same critical section)\\n\\nDeltaFIFO accumulates all changes to an object as a Deltas slice, allowing consumers to see the complete history of changes while the queue was processing.\\n\\n**4. Controller (tools/cache/controller.go):**\\nLow-level controller that orchestrates Reflector and DeltaFIFO. Key methods:\\n- Run(): Creates Reflector with the ListerWatcher and Queue, starts Reflector.Run() and processLoop()\\n- processLoop(): Continuously calls Queue.Pop() with the Process function\\n- The Process function extracts Deltas and calls processDeltas()\\n- processDeltas(handler, store, deltas): Iterates through each Delta and:\\n  - Updates the local store (indexer)\\n  - Calls handler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList) for Added/Sync/Replaced deltas\\n  - Calls handler.OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj) for Updated deltas on existing objects\\n  - Calls handler.OnDelete(obj) for Deleted deltas\\n\\n**5. SharedIndexInformer (tools/cache/shared_informer.go):**\\nImplements SharedInformer interface and acts as the main event handler. Key components:\\n- sharedIndexInformer struct: Contains indexer (cache.Store) and sharedProcessor\\n- HandleDeltas(obj): Called by processDeltas via controller, receives Deltas from DeltaFIFO, calls processDeltas() which invokes OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete\\n- OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList): Updates indexer and calls processor.distribute(addNotification{newObj, isInInitialList}, false)\\n- OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj): Updates indexer and calls processor.distribute(updateNotification{oldObj, newObj}, isSync)\\n- OnDelete(obj): Updates indexer and calls processor.distribute(deleteNotification{oldObj}, false)\\n\\n**6. SharedProcessor (tools/cache/shared_informer.go):**\\nResponsible for dispatching notifications to all registered event listeners. Key methods:\\n- distribute(notification, sync): Iterates through all listeners (processorListener instances) and calls listener.add(notification)\\n- Each listener receives the notification asynchronously\\n\\n**7. ProcessorListener (tools/cache/shared_informer.go):**\\nRelays notifications from sharedProcessor to one ResourceEventHandler using two goroutines and channels. Key components:\\n- handler: The actual ResourceEventHandler registered by the user (implements OnAdd, OnUpdate, OnDelete)\\n- addCh: Receives notifications from processor.distribute()\\n- nextCh: Buffers notifications for the run() goroutine\\n- pendingNotifications: Ring buffer for notifications not yet dispatched\\n\\nKey goroutines:\\n- pop(): Pumps notifications from addCh to nextCh using the ring buffer, handling backpressure when nextCh is not keeping up\\n- run(): Receives notifications from nextCh and dispatches them:\\n  - addNotification → calls handler.OnAdd(newObj, isInInitialList)\\n  - updateNotification → calls handler.OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj)\\n  - deleteNotification → calls handler.OnDelete(oldObj)\\n\\n**Complete Event Flow:**\\n1. API Server streams watch events → ListWatch.Watch() receives events\\n2. Reflector.watch() calls handleAnyWatch() to consume events\\n3. handleAnyWatch() calls store.Add/Update/Delete() for each watch event (DeltaFIFO)\\n4. DeltaFIFO creates Delta objects and enqueues them\\n5. Controller.processLoop() pops Deltas from DeltaFIFO\\n6. processDeltas() processes each Delta and calls sharedIndexInformer.OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete\\n7. sharedIndexInformer updates indexer (cache) and calls processor.distribute()\\n8. processor sends notifications to all processorListeners\\n9. processorListener.pop() buffers notifications, processorListener.run() dispatches them\\n10. Finally calls user's registered ResourceEventHandler methods (OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete)\\n\\nThis multi-stage pipeline with buffering, synchronization points, and handler isolation ensures that:\\n- Watch events are reliably processed\\n- The local cache is always consistent\\n- Event handlers run asynchronously and independently\\n- Multiple handlers can be registered without blocking each other\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
